Similarly, Bill Gates has expressed concerns about the possibility of a major war, citing the current unrest in the world as a potential spark [8].

In the event of a world war 3, global trade would likely plummet, and supply chains would be severely disrupted. As noted in Source 2, a scenario of global escalation would result in a significant decline in global trade, and supply chains would become increasingly localized [2]. This would lead to shortages of essential goods, including food and medicine, and would have a devastating impact on the global economy. Furthermore, the proliferation of regional conflicts would lead to a shift in trade flows, and sanctions would complicate capital flows, further exacerbating the economic crisis [2].

The consequences of a world war 3 would also be felt in the realm of geopolitics. As noted in Source 1, the advent of nuclear weapons has made it possible for even minor inventions and feints in the field of nuclear weapons to be decisive in a short amount of time [1]. This would lead to a highly unstable and unpredictable global environment, where the risk of nuclear war would be ever-present. Moreover, the rise of protectionist industrial policies and the decline of global cooperation would lead to a fragmented world, where nations would be increasingly isolated and hostile towards one another [2]. In such a scenario, the world would be a very different place, with far-reaching consequences for global politics, economies, and societies.
